Task instruction sent to agent 
# Data Flow Q&A: Envoy Request Routing

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Task Type:** Data Flow Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Envoy is a high-performance proxy that routes HTTP requests from downstream clients to upstream services. Understanding the complete path from the initial TCP accept through filter processing to the final upstream connection is critical for working with Envoy's architecture.

## Task

Trace the complete path of a single HTTP request from the moment a downstream client TCP connection is accepted through filter chain processing, route resolution, upstream cluster selection, and connection establishment. Identify every key transformation point, component boundary crossing, and state change.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Envoy's request routing flow:

### Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain

When a downstream client establishes a TCP connection to Envoy, how does the request travel from socket accept to network filter processing?

- Which component accepts the incoming TCP connection?
- How does Envoy select which network filter chain to apply based on connection properties?
- At what point does the connection get handed to the HTTP Connection Manager (HCM)?
- What triggers the initial `onData()` call when bytes arrive?

### Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration

Once bytes arrive at the HCM, how does Envoy parse HTTP and iterate through filters?

- How does the codec parse the byte stream into HTTP headers/body?
- When is the `ActiveStream` created and how does it relate to filter iteration?
- How does the `FilterManager` determine the order of decoder filter execution?
- What filter return values can stop or continue iteration?

### Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection

When the router filter is invoked, how does it select the upstream destination?

- How does the router determine which route configuration to use?
- What is the sequence of operations that resolves a route entry to a specific upstream cluster?
- How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?
- What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?

### Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow

Once an upstream host is selected, how does Envoy establish the connection and forward the request?

- How does the connection pool provide or create an upstream connection?
- What component actually writes the HTTP request to the upstream socket?
- How does the response flow back from upstream through the filter chain?
- At what points does the encoder filter chain get invoked vs. the decoder filter chain?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

```
# Envoy Request Routing Flow

## Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Evidence
<consolidated list of supporting file paths and line references>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Cite specific files, classes, and methods — avoid vague or speculative answers
- Focus on the core request path, not error handling or edge cases
- Trace a single successful HTTP/1.1 request without TLS termination

   177→  // too many open connections, and this upstream has no connections, always create one, to
   178→  // prevent pending streams being queued to this upstream with no way to be processed.

using Envoy::Router::GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks;

namespace Envoy {
namespace Extensions {
namespace Upstreams {
namespace Http {
namespace Http {

void HttpConnPool::newStream(GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks* callbacks) {
  callbacks_ = callbacks;
  // It's possible for a reset to happen inline within the newStream() call. In this case, we
  // might get deleted inline as well. Only write the returned handle out if it is not nullptr to
  // deal with this case.
  Envoy::Http::ConnectionPool::Cancellable* handle =
      pool_data_.value().newStream(callbacks->upstreamToDownstream(), *this,
                                   callbacks->upstreamToDownstream().upstreamStreamOptions());
  if (handle) {
    conn_pool_stream_handle_ = handle;
  }
}

bool HttpConnPool::cancelAnyPendingStream() {
  if (conn_pool_stream_handle_) {
    conn_pool_stream_handle_->cancel(ConnectionPool::CancelPolicy::Default);
    conn_pool_stream_handle_ = nullptr;
    return true;
  }
  return false;
}

   394→void ConnectionImpl::onRead(uint64_t read_buffer_size) {
   395→  ASSERT(dispatcher_.isThreadSafe());
   396→  // Do not read the data from the socket if the connection is in delay closed,
   397→  // high watermark is called, or is closing through filter manager.
   398→  if (inDelayedClose() || !filterChainWantsData() ||
   399→      (enable_close_through_filter_manager_ && filter_manager_.pendingClose())) {
   400→    return;
   401→  }
   402→  ASSERT(socket_->isOpen());
   403→
   404→  if (read_buffer_size == 0 && !read_end_stream_) {
   405→    return;
   406→  }
   407→
   408→  if (read_end_stream_) {
   409→    // read() on a raw socket will repeatedly return 0 (EOF) once EOF has
   410→    // occurred, so filter out the repeats so that filters don't have
   411→    // to handle repeats.
   412→    //
   413→    // I don't know of any cases where this actually happens (we should stop
   414→    // reading the socket after EOF), but this check guards against any bugs
   415→    // in ConnectionImpl or strangeness in the OS events (epoll, kqueue, etc)
   416→    // and maintains the guarantee for filters.
   417→    if (read_end_stream_raised_) {
   418→      // No further data can be delivered after end_stream
   419→      ASSERT(read_buffer_size == 0);
   420→      return;
   421→    }
   422→    read_end_stream_raised_ = true;
   423→  }
   424→
   425→  filter_manager_.onRead();
   426→}

157-assistanttext-
The investigation is complete. Here's a summary of what I traced:

## Summary of Envoy HTTP/1.1 Request Routing Flow

### Q1: Listener Accept → Network Filter Chain

1. **`ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()`** (`active_tcp_listener.cc:80`) — OS fires; connection-limit check runs, then `onAcceptWorker()` may rebalance to another worker.
2. **`ActiveTcpSocket::continueFilterChain()`** (`active_tcp_socket.cc:111`) — runs listener filters (TLS Inspector, etc.) via `onAccept()`. When all pass, calls `newConnection()`.
3. **`ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`** (`active_stream_listener_base.cc:38`) — calls `filterChainManager().findFilterChain()` which walks a 6-level trie (dest port → dest IP → SNI → transport protocol → ALPN → source IP/port).
4. **`createNetworkFilterChain()`** (`:68`) — instantiates the HCM as a `Network::ReadFilter` on the connection.
5. **`ConnectionImpl::onReadReady()`** (`connection_impl.cc:699`) — libevent fires on readable socket; `doRead()` drains bytes, then `FilterManagerImpl::onRead()` calls `filter->onData()` on the HCM.

### Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration

1. **`ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()`** (`conn_manager_impl.cc:486`) — lazily creates the HTTP/1.1 codec, then calls `codec_->dispatch(data)`.
2. **`ServerConnectionImpl::onMessageBeginBase()`** (`http1/codec_impl.cc:1266`) — codec calls `callbacks_.newStream()` which creates an **`ActiveStream`** with its `FilterManager`.
3. **`FilterManager::decodeHeaders()`** (`filter_manager.cc:537`) — iterates `decoder_filters_` in config order, calling `decodeHeaders()` on each. Return values `Continue`/`StopIteration`/`StopAllIterationAndBuffer` control progression.

### Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection

1. **`Router::Filter::decodeHeaders()`** (`router.cc:445`) — calls `ca
... (truncated)

One is listener filter\n          // needs to wait for data. The other is listener filter with 0 maxReadBytes()\n          // doesn't inspect data, but needs to wait for some asynchronous callback and\n          // listener filter buffer needs to listen for socket close event.\n          if (listener_filter_buffer_ == nullptr) {\n            createListenerFilterBuffer();\n          }\n          if ((*iter_)->maxReadBytes() > 0) {\n            listener_filter_buffer_->disableOnDataCallback(false);\n            // If the current filter expect more data than previous filters, then\n            // increase the filter buffer's capacity.\n            if (listener_filter_buffer_->capacity() < (*iter_)->maxReadBytes()) {\n              listener_filter_buffer_->resetCapacity((*iter_)->maxReadBytes());\n            }\n            if (listener_filter_buffer_ != nullptr) {\n              // There are two cases for activate event manually: One is\n              // the data is already available when connect, activate the read event to peek\n              // data from the socket . Another one is the data already\n              // peeked into the buffer when previous filter processing the data, then activate the\n              // read event to trigger the current filter callback to process the data.\n              listener_filter_buffer_->activateFileEvent(Event::FileReadyType::Read);\n            }\n          } else {\n            listener_filter_buffer_->disableOnDataCallback(true);\n          }\n\n          return;\n        }\n      }\n    }\n    // Successfully ran all the accept filters.\n    if (no_error) {\n      newConnection();\n    } else {\n      // Signal the caller that no extra filter chain iteration is needed.\n      iter_ = accept_filters_.end();\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Filter execution concluded, unlink and delete this ActiveTcpSocket if it was linked.\n  if (inserted()) {\n    unlink();\n  }\n}\n\nvoid ActiveTcpSocket::setDynamicMetadata(const std::string& name,\n              const ProtobufWkt::Any& value) {\n  stream_info_->setDynamicTypedMetadata(name, value);\n}\n\nvoid ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection() {\n  connected_ = true;\n\n  // Check if the socket may need to be redirected to another listener.\n  Network::BalancedConnectionHandlerOptRef new_listener;\n\n  if (hand_off_restored_destination_connections_ &&\n      socket_->connectionInfoProvider().localAddressRestored()) {\n    // Find a listener associated with the original destination address.\n    new_listener =\n        listener_.getBalancedHandlerByAddress(*socket_->connectionInfoProvider().localAddress());\n  }\n\n  // Reset the file events which are registered by listener filter.\n  // reference https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/8925.\n  if (listener_filter_buffer_ != nullptr) {\n    listener_filter_buffer_->reset();\n  }\n\n  if (new_listener.has_value()) {\n    // Hands off connections redirected by iptables to the listener associated with the\n    // original destination address. Pass 'hand_off_restored_destination_connections' as false to\n    // prevent further redirection.\n    // Leave the new listener to decide whether to execute re-balance.\n    // Note also that we must account for the number of connections properly across both listeners.\n    // TODO(mattklein123): See note in ~ActiveTcpSocket() related to making this accounting better.\n    listener_.decNumConnections();\n    new_listener.value().get().onAcceptWorker(std::move(socket_), false, false);\n  } else {\n    // Set default transport protocol if none of the listener filters did it.\n    if (socket_->detectedTransportProtocol().empty()) {\n      socket_->setDetectedTransportProtocol(\"raw_buffer\");\n    }\n    accept_filters_.clear();\n    // Create a new connection on this listener.\n    listener_.newConnection(std::move(socket_), std::move(stream_info_));\n  }\n}\n} // namespace Server\n} // namespace Envoy\n",

When all listener filters\nhave passed, `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` is called\n(`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc:185`), which calls\n`ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`.\n\nInside `newConnection()`\n(`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:38`), the filter chain is selected\nby calling:\n```cpp\nconst auto filter_chain = config_->filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info);\n```\n`FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()`\n(`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.cc:514`) walks a multi-level trie in\npriority order:\n\n1. **Destination port** \u2192 `destination_ports_map_`\n2. **Destination IP / CIDR** \u2192 `findFilterChainForDestinationIP()` (`:563`)\n3. **Server name (SNI)** \u2192 `findFilterChainForServerName()` (`:580`)\n4. **Transport protocol** \u2192 `findFilterChainForTransportProtocol()` (`:611`)\n5. **Application protocol (ALPN)** \u2192 `findFilterChainForApplicationProtocols()` (`:631`)\n6. **Source IP / port** \u2192 `findFilterChainForSourceIpAndPort()` (`:702`)\n\nIf a matcher-based config is present, `findFilterChainUsingMatcher()` (`:549`) is used instead.\n\n### At what point does the connection get handed to the HCM?\n\nAfter `findFilterChain()` returns a non-null `FilterChain`, `newConnection()` calls:\n```cpp\nconfig_->filterChainFactory().createNetworkFilterChain(*server_conn_ptr,\n                                                        filter_chain->networkFilterFactories());\n```\n(`active_stream_listener_base.cc:68`)\n\nThis instantiates the HCM (`ConnectionManagerImpl`) as a `ReadFilter` and registers it on the\n`ServerConnectionImpl` via `FilterManagerImpl::addReadFilter()`\n(`source/common/network/filter_manager_impl.cc:25`). On first call it lazily creates the codec via\n`createCodec(data)` (`:465`) which calls `config_->createCodec()` and stores the result in\n`codec_`. Parsed events map to\ncallbacks:\n- `onMessageBeginBase()` (`:1266`) \u2014 called when the HTTP request-line is received. The `ActiveStream` owns\nan `Http::FilterManager` which holds the ordered decoder-filter and encoder-filter lists.\n\nWhen the codec calls `request_decoder->decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)`, this invokes\n`FilterManager::decodeHeaders()`, which iterates decoder filters.\n\n### How does the `FilterManager` determine the order of decoder filter execution?\n\n`FilterManager` maintains `decoder_filters_` as a `std::list<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr>` built\nin insertion order by `addStreamDecoderFilter()`. Filters are added in configuration order during\n`createFilterChain()` (HCM config). Iteration starts from the front (first configured filter) via\n`commonDecodePrefix()` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:537`), which picks either the current\nfilter or the next one depending on from `decodeHeaders`:\n\n| Value | Effect |\n|---|---|\n| `Continue` | Advance to next decoder filter |\n| `StopIteration` | Pause at current filter (`StopSingleIteration`), resume via `continueDecoding()` |\n| `StopAllIterationAndBuffer` | Buffer data and stop all iteration |\n| `StopAllIterationAndWatermark` | As above but also apply watermark pressure |\n| `ContinueAndDontEndStream` | Continue but clear `end_stream` (converts header-only to header+body) |\n\nThese are handled in `ActiveStreamFilterBase::commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback()`\n(`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:130`).\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection\n\n### How does the router `RouteConfigImpl::route()` performs virtual-host lookup by\n`Host` header, then route matching against the path/method/headers, returning a `RouteEntry*`.\n\n### What is the sequence of operations `config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName())` \u2014 look up the\n   `ThreadLocalCluster` by name from `ClusterManager` (`:519`).\n3. `cluster_ = cluster->info()` \u2014 snapshot the cluster's `ClusterInfo` (`:530`).\n4. `cluster->chooseHost(this)` \u2014 run the load-balancer to pick an `Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr`\n   (`:664`). This invokes the cluster's `LoadBalancer` (e.g. RoundRobin, LeastRequest) using the\n   `LoadBalancerContext` provided by the router filter.\n5. `createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host)` \u2014 obtain or create a `GenericConnPool` (`:724`).\n\n### How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?\n\n`cluster->chooseHost(this)` delegates to the cluster's thread-local `LoadBalancer::chooseHost()`.\nThe load balancer selects from `ready` host entries in the cluster's priority set, applying the\nconfigured policy (round-robin, least-request, random, etc.) along with health-check and\nlocality-weight information. The result is a `HostConstSharedPtr`.\n\n### What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?\n\n`Filter::createConnPool()` (`source/common/router/router.cc:905`) calls\n`factory->createGenericConnPool(host, cluster, upstream_protocol, ...)` (`:946`). Decoder filters run in\nconfiguration order (front-to-back) on incoming request data. 1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Envoy Request Routing Flow

## Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain

### Which component accepts the incoming TCP connection?

The kernel delivers the `accept()` event to the `TcpListenerImpl` (libevent-backed) which fires an
`onAccept` callback on **`ActiveTcpListener`**
(`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc:80`).

`ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` does a connection-limit check, then delegates to
`ActiveTcpListener::onAcceptWorker()` (`:108`), which may rebalance the connection to another worker
thread via `ConnectionBalancer::pickTargetHandler()`. If the connection stays on the same worker, an
`ActiveTcpSocket` is created and handed to `ActiveStreamListenerBase::onSocketAccepted()`.

### How does Envoy select which network filter chain to apply based on connection properties?

`ActiveTcpSocket::continueFilterChain()` runs any configured **listener filters**
(e.g. `TLS Inspector`, `HTTP Inspector`) via `(*iter_)->onAccept(*this)`. When all listener filters
have passed, `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` is called
(`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc:185`), which calls
`ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`.

Inside `newConnection()`
(`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:38`), the filter chain is selected
by calling:
```cpp
const auto filter_chain = config_->filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info);
```
`FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()`
(`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.cc:514`) walks a multi-level trie in
priority order:

1. **Destination port** → `destination_ports_map_`
2. **Destination IP / CIDR** → `findFilterChainForDestinationIP()` (`:563`)
3. **Server name (SNI)** → `findFilterChainForServerName()` (`:580`)
4. **Transport protocol** → `f
... (truncated)
